The push toward affordable 5G devices is clearly as much an indicator as the current state of the smartphone space as anything — people just aren’t upgrading devices as quickly as the used to. And even more to the point, they’re reluctant to pay $1,000 when they do.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\">Qualcomm’s Snapdragon 765G has been a piece of that puzzle. And unsurprisingly, the mid-tier chip in found in TCL’s new $400 5G handset. Of course, TCL is positioning it as “under-$400” with that $399.99 price tag, which is technically correct — the best kind of correct.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"b2tzh3Gz8Z\"><p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/21/nord-is-onepluss-sub-500-5g-handset/\">Nord is OnePlus&#8217;s sub-$500 5G handset</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Nord is OnePlus&#8217;s sub-$500 5G handset&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/21/nord-is-onepluss-sub-500-5g-handset/embed/#?secret=b2tzh3Gz8Z\" data-secret=\"b2tzh3Gz8Z\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p class=\"p1\">It’s also not really right to say that the TCL 10 5G UW’s a”premium blend of performance, power, stylish design and 5G connectivity that until now has only been available on more expensive flagship smartphones.” Affordable 5G handsets isn&#8217;t an entirely new phenomenon &#8212; nor are affordable 5G handsets with decent specs and design. But even so, the price point is still notable at this stage in the 5G upgrade cycle — which, frankly, is why we’re writing about it here.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\">The price/5G combo is the main thing to like here, coming in at even less than, say, the OnePlus Nord, a recent high water mark in the 5G/price point combo. And there are a few other things that should appeal to potential buyers, as well, including a 4,500mAh battery coupled with reverse charging for other devices. There are three rear-facing cameras: a 48-megapixel main, an eight-megapixel ultra wide and a five-megapixel macro, the latter of of which is starting to appear on more phones.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\">It arrives October 29, and is, notably, a Verizon (TechCrunch’s parent company) exclusive here in the U.S., using the carrier’s mmWave technology.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote 00:53:35","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","title":"Lightyear scores $3.7M seed to digitize networking infrastructure procurement","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2066083","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"http://lightyear.ai\">Lightyear</a>, a New York City startup that wants to make it easier for large companies to procure networking infrastructure like internet and SD-WAN, announced a $3.7 million seed round today.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/amplo\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"amplo\">Amplo <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> led the round with help from Susa Ventures, Ludlow Ventures, Mark Cuban, David Adelman and Operator Partners. While it was at it, the company announced that it was emerging from stealth and offering its solution in public beta.</p>\n<p>Company CEO and co-founder Dennis Thankachan says that while so much technology buying has moved online, networking technology procurement still involves phone calls for price quotes that could sometimes take weeks to get. Thankachan says that when he was working at a hedge fund specializing in telecommunications he witnessed this first hand and saw an opportunity for a startup to fill the void.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;Our objective is to make the process of buying telecom infrastructure, kind of like buying socks on Amazon, providing a real consumer-like experience to the enterprise and empowering buyers with data because information asymmetry and a lack of transparent data on what things should cost, where providers are available, and even what&#8217;s existing already in your network is really at the core of the problem for why this is frustrating for enterprise buyers,&#8221; Thankachan explained.</p>\n<p>The company offers the ability to simply select a service and find providers in your area with costs and contract terms if it&#8217;s a simple purchase, but he recognizes that not all enterprise purchases will be that simple and the startup is working to digitize the corporate buying process into the <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/lightyear\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"lightyear\">Lightyear <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> platform.</p>\n<p>To provide the data that he spoke of, the company has already formed relationships with over 400 networking providers worldwide. The pricing model is in flux, but could involve a monthly subscription or a percentage of the sale. That is something they are working out, but they are using the latter during beta testing to keep the product free for now.</p>\n<p>The company already has 10 employees and flush with the new investment, it plans to double that in the next year. Thankachan says as he builds the company, particularly as a person of color himself, he takes diversity and inclusion extremely seriously and sees it as part of the company&#8217;s core values.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Trying to enable people from non-traditional backgrounds to succeed will be really important to us, and I think providing economic opportunity to people that traditionally would not have been afforded several aspects of economic opportunity is the biggest ways to fix the opportunity gap in this country,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>The company, which launched a year ago has basically grown up during the pandemic. That means he has yet to meet any of his customers or investors in person, but he says he has learned to adapt to that approach. While he is based in NYC, his investors are are in the Bay Area and so that remote approach will remain in place for the time being.</p>\n<p>As he makes his way from seed to a Series A, he says that it&#8217;s up to him to stay focused and execute with the goal of showing product-market fit across a variety of company types. He believes if the startup can do this, it will have the data to take to investors when it&#8217;s time to take the next step.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a testers","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2066285","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/space-exploration-technologies\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"space-exploration-technologies\">SpaceX <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has debuted an official app for its Starlink satellite broadband internet service, for both iOS and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/android\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"android\">Android <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> devices. The Starlink app allows users to manage their connection – but to take part you&#8217;ll have to be part of the official beta program, and the initial public rollout of that is only just about to begin, according to emails SpaceX sent to potential beta testers this week.</p>\n<p>The Starlink app provides guidance on how to install the Starlink receiver dish, as well as connection status (including signal quality), a device overview for seeing what&#8217;s connected to your network, and a speed test tool. It&#8217;s similar to other mobile apps for managing home wifi connections and routers. Meanwhile, the emails to potential testers that <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/10/27/spacex-starlink-service-priced-at-99-a-month-public-beta-test-begins.html\">CNBC obtained</a> detail what users can expect in terms of pricing, speeds and latency.</p>\n<p>The initial Starlink public beta test is called the &#8220;Better than Nothing Beta Program,&#8221; SpaceX confirms in their app description, and will be rolled out across the U.S. and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/canada-c0c7\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"canada-c0c7\">Canada <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> before the end of the year – which matches up with earlier stated timelines. As per the name, SpaceX is hoping to set expectations for early customers, with speeds users can expect ranging from between 50Mb/s to 150Mb/s, and latency of 20ms to 40ms according to the customer emails, with some periods including no connectivity at all. Even with expectations set low, if those values prove accurate, it should be a big improvement for users in some hard-to-reach areas where service is currently costly, unreliable and operating at roughly dial-up equivalent speeds.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2066317\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2066317\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2066317\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Starlink-UT.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"575\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Starlink-UT.jpg 1390w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Starlink-UT.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Starlink-UT.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Starlink-UT.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Starlink-UT.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Starlink-UT.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2066317\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> SpaceX</p></div></p>\n<p>In terms of pricing, SpaceX says in the emails that the cost for participants in this beta program will be $99 per moth, plus a one-time cost of $499 initially to pay for the hardware, which includes the mounting kit and receiver dish, as well as a router with wifi networking capabilities.</p>\n<p>The goal eventually is offer reliably, low-latency broadband that provides consistent connection by handing off connectivity between a large constellation of small satellites circling the globe in low Earth orbit. Already, SpaceX has nearly 1,000 of those launched, but it hopes to launch many thousands more before it reaches global coverage and offers general availability of its services.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"DbylYIxLk7\"><p><a showing low latency and speeds over 100Mbps</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;SpaceX confirms Starlink programs for Starlink, too, including a team-up with <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/microsoft\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"microsoft\">Microsoft <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> to connect that company&#8217;s mobile Azure data centers, and a project with an East Texas school board to 00:53:35","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","title":"Upstream aims to be the new home for your professional social life","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2066131","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Last fall, social analytics startup <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/19/trufan-acquires-socialrank/\">SocialRank sold its product and business to Trufan</a>, allowing the team to focus on something new: a professional social network. Today, they&#8217;re officially unveiling <a href=\"https://upstreamapp.com\">Upstream</a> to the public.</p>\n<p>To be clear, CEO Alex Taub told me that he&#8217;s not trying to replace LinkedIn — he acknowledged that thanks to network effects,&#8221;If you want to go and try to take down LinkedIn, you&#8217;re not going to be able to take them down.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Instead, the goal is to create something that fulfills a different need. Where LinkedIn works primarily as an online résumé and rolodex, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/upstream-systems\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"upstream-systems\">Upstream <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> aims to help users build the connections and relationships that are important to their careers — something that&#8217;s sorely needed at a time when large-scale meetups and conferences aren&#8217;t really possible (though we&#8217;re certainly trying to create the virtual equivalent <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/events/\">at TechCrunch</a>).</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;This is the place for your professional social life,&#8221; Taub said.</p>\n<p>Upstream&#8217;s first product focused on professional groups and communities, allowing users to post what the company called Professional Asks, like if they&#8217;re looking to hire someone for a certain position or need an introduction at another company.</p>\n<p>Taub suggested that things really took off with Upstream&#8217;s next product, Upstream Events, where Upstream would host a guest speaker, then attendees were matched up for five-minute, one-on-one video chats with the other people at the event.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2066229\" style=\"width: 349px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2066229\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2066229\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1I8VBjurgpR3PY2z7iWs83Q.jpg?w=339\" alt=\"Upstream\" width=\"339\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1I8VBjurgpR3PY2z7iWs83Q.jpg 711w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1I8VBjurgpR3PY2z7iWs83Q.jpg?resize=75,150 75w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1I8VBjurgpR3PY2z7iWs83Q.jpg?resize=150,300 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1I8VBjurgpR3PY2z7iWs83Q.jpg?resize=339,680 339w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1I8VBjurgpR3PY2z7iWs83Q.jpg?resize=25,50 25w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 339px) 100vw, 339px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2066229\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Upstream</p></div></p>\n<p>Upstream says it&#8217;s already hosted more than 100 events, with 72% of people who who attend one event subsequently attending another.</p>\n<p>While the team has built multiple products (and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/24/former-founders-of-socialrank-have-launched-a-job-board-for-covid-19-layoffs/\">we&#8217;ve covered some of them</a> already), they&#8217;re outlining the broader vision today and launching some new features at the same time.</p>\n<p>For one thing, while communities were previously shared via a private, unlisted link, you can now browse all the different communities in a Discovery section. At the same time, community organizers will be still be able to control who joins by approving or rejecting new members.</p>\n<p>There&#8217;s also a new spin on Events called Office Hours, allowing users to set aside structured time for virtual one-on-one sessions with anyone who&#8217;s interested in speaking to them. These sessions can be listed publicly, or they can be unlisted, so that you only share them via email or within a certain community.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2066231\" style=\"width: 348px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2066231\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical size-large wp-image-2066231\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg?w=338\" alt=\"Upstream screenshot\" width=\"338\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg 805w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg?resize=75,150 75w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg?resize=149,300 149w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg?resize=768,1544 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg?resize=338,680 338w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg?resize=764,1536 764w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg?resize=25,50 25w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 338px) 100vw, 338px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2066231\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Upstream</p></div></p>\n<p>In <a href=\"https://joinupstream.medium.com/introducing-upstream-4303d0968e9\">a blog post</a>, Taub noted that he met his SocialRank/Upstream co-founder and CTO Michael Schonfeld via Ohours.org, and they&#8217;re trying to replicate that experience here:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Let’s say you are the CMO of a large company and you want to give your people the opportunity to meet 1:1. The thought of coordinating the individual scheduling of ten minute blocks using your Outlook calendar and email is not attractive. But with Upstream, you are able to choose the 30min block you want to offer and how long you want the sessions to be. You decide you want to run your office hours every other Friday at 2pm ET for the rest of the year. The event is built and able to be shared seamlessly to whoever you choose to offer the Office Hours to.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In fact, Taub&#8217;s post lists more than 30 different people who are already offering office hours on Upstream, including New York Times reporter <a href=\"https://upstreamapp.com/officeHours/R7C3OWTDo8?_branch_match_id=684774800918594150\">Taylor Lorenz</a>, Foursquare co-founder/Expa partner <a href=\"https://upstreamapp.com/officeHours/-ICitpi9mq?_branch_match_id=684774800918594150\">Naveen Selvadurai</a> and Amazon Photo Head of Product <a href=\"https://upstreamapp.com/officeHours/vpqfTHkKiJ?_branch_match_id=684774800918594150\">Nate Westheiemer</a>.</p>\n<p>Upstream is also announcing that it has raised an undisclosed amount of pre-seed funding from 8-Bit Capital, Human Ventures, Basement Fund, NYVP and various angel investors.</p>\n<p>Looking ahead, Taub said that the next big priority is launching a web version of Upstream (which is currently available via mobile app), and to continue building live experiences, asynchronous experiences and features that provide real utility.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We imagine a future when professionals come to Upstream for an event or Ask, and stay for the compelling opportunities that make Upstream an energizing and beneficial experience for them,&#8221; he wrote.</p>\n<div Ha","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1I8VBjurgpR3PY2z7iWs83Q.jpg?w=339":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn4@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-53-36-202_63d337ebb9006958.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1QvQyhv7F4sgCdb8lrrb7Zw.jpg?w=338":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn89@2020_6/2020/10/27/16-54-15-683_1cfac6e5070bc2cc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn36@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-53-36-082_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn80@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn32@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-14-449_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Ktj0z0wsuH0:TzpxT1YJX8Y:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn96@2020_1/2020/10/27/16-54-14-607_3fb68f29d029b44f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Ktj0z0wsuH0:TzpxT1YJX8Y:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn20@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-14-536_556486cdc212b158.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn14@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-676_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/Ktj0z0wsuH0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn40@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-14-589_b761ba3a51a9b4ec.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817615700},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","title":"SpaceX and LeoLabs partner up for tracking of Starlink satellite deployments","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2066183","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/space-exploration-technologies\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"space-exploration-technologies\">SpaceX <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and orbital object tracking startup LeoLabs have announced a new commercial partnership that will see LeoLab track SpaceX&#8217;s Starlink satellites during their initial deployment and orbital travel. The arrangement means that LeoLabs will immediately start tracking new Starlink satellites once they&#8217;re released in space following a launch, giving <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/space-exploration-technologies\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"space-exploration-technologies\">SpaceX <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> immediate info in terms of placement and trajectory during the crucial initial few days of any new batch launch.</p>\n<p>LeoLabs&#8217; provides an advantage vs. any other options out there in terms of how fast it can acquire signal from a whole batch of newly orbital Starlink satellites, which SpaceX has been sending up in batches of 60. Here&#8217;s a brief synopsis of what exactly LeoLabs is doing for SpaceX through this arrangement, <a href=\"https://medium.com/@leolabs_space/leolabs-partners-with-spacex-to-track-starlink-satellite-deployments-4e579052546f\">straight from the company itself</a>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>LeoLabs tracks all Starlink satellites (up to 60 per launch) and rapidly generates data products on the front and back of the cluster to provide a bounding box on the train of satellites. This begins within the first few hours following launch and deployment. We continue to monitor the satellites in the following hours and days as they disperse and begin their orbit raising sequences.</p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The actual operational partnership has been active since March of this year, which means that LeoLabs has been tracking these deployments for a number of missions thus far. It&#8217;s also going to continue to do this for future launches going forward. Through their platform, SpaceX gets timely data on Starlink satellites and their orbits just a few hours post-launch, and the startup says it can typically deliver data within one hour of a Starlink satellite passing over one of its radar stations.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2066201\" style=\"width: 610px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2066201\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2066201\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1iVpIxiR90-9OcKt4ohtwPg.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"373\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2066201\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> LeoLabs</p></div></p>\n<p>LeoLabs has made headlines recently tracking potential collisions among objects in low Earth orbit, including most recently a near-collision with an 11-meter miss of two objects earlier this month. As low Earth orbit becomes more crowded – in no small part due to SpaceX&#8217;s planned massive increase in its Starlink fleet size – the company&#8217;s services are likely to only grow in demand in order to help with effective space traffic control.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=XJOpNkTJDiw:2ixZLnx82rs:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=XJOpNkTJDiw:2ixZLnx82rs:7Q72WNTAKBA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=XJOpNkTJDiw:2ixZLnx82rs:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img And <a href=\"https://www.pleaseassistme.com/\">Please Assist Me</a> is pretty spot-on for my generation&#8217;s yuppies.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=dOUj28E8QIs:C-2LAli4SsM:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/dOUj28E8QIs\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 27 Oct 2020 14:17:46 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-blu.jpg?w=300","linkMd5":"ff48bc63a97816119fe9a84e3f5914e6","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn16@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-53-36-092_1ba81e7e68c3a2fe.webp","destWidth":300,"destHeight":300,"sourceBytes":31720,"destBytes":31720,"author":"Alex Wilhelm","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-blu.jpg?w=300":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn16@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-53-36-092_1ba81e7e68c3a2fe.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn36@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-53-36-082_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn80@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn32@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-14-449_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=dOUj28E8QIs:C-2LAli4SsM:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn91@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-54-14-555_97c36da8551a07c5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=dOUj28E8QIs:C-2LAli4SsM:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn26@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-15-836_581528c11210510f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn14@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-676_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/dOUj28E8QIs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn11@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-14-567_f213b787a9a5bb9f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817615706},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","title":"Hands-on: Sony’s DualSense PS5 controller could be a game changer","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2065758","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">After spending a few hours with the PlayStation 5 and its completely redesigned DualSense controller, I can say with confidence that the new haptics and audio features certainly work — and could become integral to the gaming experience. But only if — and it&#8217;s a big if — developers truly embrace the tech.</p>\n<p>The DualSense controller replaces the extremely familiar and beloved design of the DualShock, which has remained largely the same shape since the first one shipped for the original PlayStation 25 years ago.</p>\n<p>While the general layout is the same, the feel of the new controller is significantly different and the appearance is aligned with the PS5&#8217;s distinctive but questionable hyper-futuristic look. I&#8217;m not entirely sold on the new shape but I&#8217;ve also had a long time to get used to the old one, so I&#8217;m withholding judgment while I work on the full review.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Shipping with every <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/16/sonys-playstation-5-arrives-november-12-priced-at-500/\">PS5</a> is Astro&#8217;s Playroom, which like Nintendoland and Wii Sports is intended to provide a reference experience for all the controller&#8217;s new features. It may not be quite as original or persistently enjoyable as Nintendo&#8217;s pack-ins (which still number among the best games for their platforms), but it&#8217;s a fun little playroom that does a good job showing off the DualSense.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2065845\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2065845\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2065845\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg\" alt=\"A Sony DualSense controller seen from above.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"659\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg 2500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=150,97 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=300,193 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=768,494 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=680,438 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=1536,989 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=2048,1318 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/dualsense-hero.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2065845\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/sony\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"sony\">Sony</p></div></p> <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>\n<p>The first and perhaps most immediately compelling feature is the haptic feedback on the trigger buttons, L2 and R2. It&#8217;s one of those things that when you feel it working, you immediately start thinking about how it could be used.</p>\n<p>What it does is allow not just precision vibration but actual resistance to be added to the triggers, something that sounds vague in theory but is very easy to grasp, so to speak, in practice.</p>\n<p>For instance, in the setup process for Astro&#8217;s Playroom the feature is introduced by simply asking you to pull the triggers and feel it. You&#8217;ll certainly have pulled them before that, so you know that they&#8217;re nearly frictionless normally. But suddenly they&#8217;re pushing back against your finger — then a click, and the resistance is gone.</p>\n<p>&#8220;What is this sorcery?&#8221; I recall saying out loud at the time, or something like it but more profane. It really is that immediately compelling.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2065846\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2065846\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2065846\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg 1920w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/astros-playroom.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2065846\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Sony</p></div></p>\n<p>Later, in the first stage I tried of the game, your little robot jumps into a sort of spring suit (a metal spring, not a linen two-piece) and you have to pull the trigger to make it jump. The haptics in this case truly give a feel of compressing something (though, having played with springs before, I know they don&#8217;t feel like this), and importantly give you a non-visual, intuitive indicator of how far you&#8217;ve depressed the trigger. My brain was quicker to register how far I&#8217;d pulled it with the combination of sound, haptics and graphics than graphics alone. And because the feeling is localized to the trigger you&#8217;re using, there&#8217;s no confusion with the greater vibrations of the all-purpose rumble system.</p>\n<p>The Switch&#8217;s Joy-Cons have a sort of precision haptics in them, and while the demo of that feature was interesting — feeling little objects rattle around &#8220;inside&#8221; the controller — it&#8217;s actually quite hard to think of ways it could be used in gameplay. And indeed few games have done so, though to be fair rumble in general is probably better because of it.</p>\n<p>In the DualSense&#8217;s case, I was immediately thinking, &#8220;this would be great for&#8230;&#8221; and wishing I&#8217;d had it in this or that game in the past. It opens up possibilities I&#8217;ve never liked the idea of, like &#8220;pull the trigger halfway to do one thing, all the way to do another. It&#8217;s also potentially a great accessibility feature.</p>\n<p>Having a speaker and microphone in the controller is nothing new, though they appear to have been upgraded for the DualSense. Few games have been able to use these features properly, and Astro&#8217;s Playroom resorts to the old &#8220;blow on the controller to make a propeller go&#8221; thing. I can&#8217;t imagine anyone wanting to do that in any real game — but why can&#8217;t I yell &#8220;Go, cyberdog! Attack the monster on the right&#8221; to direct my (sadly fictitious) companion, or something like that?</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"M9eGJlCKxO\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/16/sonys-playstation-5-arrives-november-12-priced-at-500/\">Sony&#8217;s PlayStation 5 arrives November 12, priced at $500</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Sony&#8217;s PlayStation 5 arrives November 12, priced at $500&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/16/sonys-playstation-5-arrives-november-12-priced-at-500/embed/#?secret=M9eGJlCKxO\" data-secret=\"M9eGJlCKxO\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Unfortunately that gets to the heart of what makes even the excellent haptic feature a potentially lost cause. Developers need to design for them in a big way, and that&#8217;s difficult when you can&#8217;t guarantee that people will want or be able to use them. Not only that, but if you want to release on Xbox and PC too, you have to remove them. So they become optional features&#8230; and since they&#8217;re optional, they can&#8217;t be integrated into the game as deeply to begin with, making them less compelling overall. It&#8217;s happened over and over with various innovations gaming companies have come up with over the years, and it may happen with this generation&#8217;s gimmicks as well.</p>\n<p>Sony&#8217;s best bet is to make integration painless and highly incentivized, though it&#8217;s hard to imagine how multi-platform developers like Ubisoft can do much more than the minimum. Serious use will likely be limited to a handful of top-shelf Sony-funded PS5 exclusives that players will marvel at.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s an interesting new gameplay feature, but hardly one that screams &#8220;next-generation.&#8221; Indeed little about the next consoles from Sony or Microsoft screams that except the specs. That doesn&#8217;t mean they aren&#8217;t worth buying — but don&#8217;t expect anything transformative.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Over the last few years, it also built more <a href=\"https://panoply.io/integrations/\">code-free data integrations</a> into the platform that make it easier for businesses to pull in data from a wide variety of sources, including the likes of Salesforce, HubSpot, NetSuite, Xero, Quickbooks, Freshworks and others. Today, though, there can be little doubt that we&#8217;re in a booming market for data warehousing and analytics services. There&#8217;s nary a business left, after all, that isn&#8217;t looking to gain more insights from the copious amounts of data they gather every single day now. That market is now more competitive than ever, too, with incumbents like Snowflake, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/databricks\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"databricks\">Databricks <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and others (including all of the hyper clouds) all aiming for their slice of the market. 00:53:35","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","title":"Google confirms post-Election Day political ad ban, partners with AP on election results","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2066119","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> today <a href=\"https://blog.google/outreach-initiatives/civics/following-2020-us-election-google/\">announced</a> several updates related to how it&#8217;s helping direct people to the polls, provide election results, and help people access real-time election news across its platforms and services, like Search, Assistant and YouTube. The company said it will again partner with the Associated Press (AP) to deliver authoritative information on election results on both Google Search and Assistant. It also confirmed <a href=\"https://www.axios.com/google-to-block-election-ads-after-election-day-4b60650d-b5c2-4fb4-a856-70e30e19af17.html\">earlier</a> reports that it won&#8217;t run political ads on its platform after the polls close on November 3.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.axios.com/google-to-block-election-ads-after-election-day-4b60650d-b5c2-4fb4-a856-70e30e19af17.html\">Axios had first reported</a> on Google&#8217;s plans to ban political ads after election day, citing an email sent to advertisers. The email had told advertisers they would not be able to run ads &#8220;referencing candidates, the election, or its outcome, given that an unprecedented amount of votes will be counted after election day this year.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Google <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2020/09/25/916957090/google-to-halt-political-ads-after-polls-close-amid-worries-over-delayed-results\">confirmed</a> the move at the time of the original report by offering a statement.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Today, Google published the details of its decision in <a href=\"https://blog.google/outreach-initiatives/civics/following-2020-us-election-google/\">a company blog post</a>, saying it has chosen to enforce its <a href=\"https://support.google.com/adspolicy/answer/6015406?hl=en&#38;ref_topic=1626336\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-analytics-onclick=\"{&#34;event&#34;:&#34;page interaction&#34;,&#34;category&#34;:&#34;in-article links&#34;,&#34;action&#34;:&#34;link click&#34;,&#34;label&#34;:&#34;https://support.google.com/adspolicy/answer/6015406?hl=en&#38;ref_topic=1626336&#34;}\">Sensitive Events policy</a> as soon as the polls close on Nov. 3, given the possibility of &#8220;delayed election results this year&#8221; and to &#8220;limit the potential for ads to increase confusion post-election.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The policy, specifically, says Google does not allow:</p>\n<p><em>Ads that potentially profit from or exploit a sensitive event with significant social, cultural, or political impact, such as civil emergencies, natural disasters, public health emergencies, terrorism and related activities, conflict, or mass acts of violence</em></p>\n<p>Google isn&#8217;t the only tech giant to take aim at political advertising in this heated election season. Facebook this month <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/10/07/technology/facebook-political-ads-ban.html\">widened its ban on political ads,</a> saying those ads would be blocked indefinitely after Nov. 3. Twitter made the decision to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/15/twitter-makes-its-political-ad-ban-official/\">ban political ads last year.</a></p>\n<p>In Google&#8217;s case, it&#8217;s calling its political ad ban a &#8220;temporary pause,&#8221; and says it&#8217;s directed towards an ads referencing &#8220;the 2020 election, the candidates or its outcome.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The company also took the time today to note other voting and election-related initiatives it has underway, including its ongoing activities taking place in election seasons that help people find voter registration information and other election deadlines. It&#8217;s also <a href=\"https://blog.google/products/search/find-voting-and-ballot-drop-box-locations-google/\">directing users to voting locations</a> and ballot drop boxes on Google Maps.</p>\n<p>On YouTube, it&#8217;s pointed users to relevant election-related search results, voter registration information, and details on how to vote.</p>\n<p>This year, Google noted it will partner with the AP to provide election results in Google Search and Assistant. The companies have worked together in the past elections, too.</p>\n<p>Users will encounter a new election module with data provided by the AP when they either search for &#8220;election results&#8221; on Google Search or ask, &#8220;Hey Google, what are the current election results?&#8221; The data will include both federal and state level races across more than 70 languages, Google says.</p>\n<p>YouTube, meanwhile, <a href=\"https://blog.youtube/news-and-events/our-approach-to-election-day-on-YouTube\">will feature</a> real-time election streams from major news providers, and link to coverage on Google Search. Google News will also feature a 2020 U.S. Election <a href=\"https://news.app.goo.gl/2020_Elections_Keyword\">section</a> where users can follow both local and national news.</p>\n<div 00:53:35","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","title":"Backed by Mr. Beast and Nadeshot, Backbone One could finally crack mobile gaming","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2066256","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I get to play with a lot of new hardware from startups and it runs the gamut from super polished to barely working, neither of which is a value judgement! But every once in a while I get to mess with a new piece of kit that is just so fully realized that I am literally shocked. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Backbone One controller is one of those situations. It’s a game controller for iPhones that has slick ergonomics, solid button feel, sensitive analog triggers and great build quality. But what makes Backbone One special is the companion app and service that ships with it and enables a truly clever software layer enabling cross-app multiplayer, game recording, highlight editing and quick swap. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Designers from Ideo and Astro Studios helped realize Backbone and the pedigree of people who have crafted devices like the Xbox 360 controller really show here. Wide L1/R1 buttons make it easy to tap on mobile. Analog L2/R2 triggers feel deep but tight. The latest Lightning connector standard means extremely low latency for control signals. </span></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The controller is around 7” long in its compact state and uses a clever sliding mechanism to expand outwards to up to 10” in size. It easily fits Apple’s “Plus” sized phones and when you’re using one of those it feels like a full on game console for the first time I can remember.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There are acoustic tunneling scoops at the inside edges that direct sound forward from the phone speakers and there is work being done behind the scenes to cancel out the specific sounds the Backbone One’s buttons make so that you don’t hear those while you’re playing. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But it’s the software that makes Backbone One really special.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To co-opt a biblical phrase, hardware without software is dead. And the Backbone One is really, really alive.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Behind the Backbone One is Backbone itself, which is a ‘companion app’ but is really a live gaming service. It has integrated cross-game voice chat, game switching, parties and a friends list. It lets you get push notifications when your friends are on and slide right into a game with them with a single tap. It’s remarkably slick and feels as first-party as you could make something that is literally not first-party feel.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Backbone was founded by Maneet Khaira in the summer of 2018 while interning at YouTube and wrapping up at Columbia. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Khaira notes that one of the biggest issues in mobile gaming is that there is a ton of activation energy when it comes to jumping in and playing with friends. The major games are there: Call of Duty, Fortnite (eventually, again), PUBG &#8212; but the last mile issue is major. </span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-2066273\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg 4032w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Khaira points out that while there are plenty of examples of top-tier gaming titles on iPhone, there is just a desert of content created on these platforms available to watch on Twitch or YouTube. He likens it to a hysteresis &#8212; a lagging behind of an effect from its cause. There are </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">so many</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> mobile gamers that there should be a </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">ton</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> of mobile content shared, but because the mechanisms to do so have been so poor and so under-crafted, we have next to nothing. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Backbone changes that completely. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here are the basic pillars of Backbone:</span></p>\n<ol>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Gameplay has to feel good. The Backbone controller had to be best-in-class hardware.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Content creation. It had to be easy and seamless to capture highlights, clips and footage and share them to your preferred platform. </span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Playing with friends has to be instantaneous. Backbone uses notifications about when friends start playing across any game and you can do so from one central friends list. </span></li>\n</ol>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Because Backbone is a support app, it gets a bunch of special privileges that would normally not be granted to a ‘regular’ class of app. Backbone One is always on while it’s attached, which means that the app can do whatever it needs to do no matter what app you’re in or for how long. This is huge because it enables the Backbone button on the controller to add games to your dashboard, swap easily between them and lets you get at your friends list contained in Backbone.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The stopwatch time for attaching the Backbone One to your phone and beginning to play a game in multiplayer is measured in seconds, not minutes. It’s exactly what you need in the mobile context.</span></p>\n<p>[gallery ids=\"2066280,2066277,2066262,2066265,2066258,2066259\"]</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It also enables any-time recording of clips and highlights that store locally on your device but can be uploaded anywhere at 1080p/30fps HEVC. When you’re in game you can just smash the Capture button to start recording and tap it to screenshot. The Backbone app also has some ML work going on to identify highlight-worthy clips and mark them automatically. You can also tag them yourself while you play.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">And Backbone One does this on less power than the crap earbuds that (used to) come in an iPhone box. You won’t notice any major power drain from the accessory itself. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If Backbone can manage to get a partnership with one or two majors to have a built-in control scheme that takes advantage of the proper dead zones and timing it could be a real watershed moment for mobile gaming. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But right now it works with </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">most</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> games that have controller support right out of the box. No game needs to do anything special to take advantage of the majority of Backbone features. This basically adds on a layer of inter-game social and clip sharing. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s all of the basic features of Game Center, Twitch, PSN and Xbox Live rolled into one &#8212; but on iPhone. And, of course, the BackBone one works just fine with Xbox and PlayStation remote play apps.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-2066294\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"419\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png 5766w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png?resize=150,61 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png?resize=300,123 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png?resize=768,315 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png?resize=680,279 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png?resize=1536,629 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png?resize=2048,839 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png?resize=50,20 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Sometimes a list of investors can tell you a lot about how serious a company is about getting the right kind of money. For a company building a gaming service and peripheral hardware, Backbone couldn’t have a more solid column. Backbone is backed by MrBeast, Preston, Kwebbelkop, Typical Gamer, Night Media, Nadeshot, and Ludlow Ventures, as well as Ashton Kutcher and Guy Oseary’s Sound Ventures. Pretty much exactly the profile I would want to see for a company serious about social and mobile gaming. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In many ways, Backbone feels like a spiritual successor to <a href=\"http://www.openfeint.com/?__cf_chl_jschl_tk__=3568b04772e91c33271d8c62b8f6753062efd764-1602291618-0-AQ3hlLqj7ObQTsCxKRMNjIBbP01TwQSTluv7I9LZksLLSfBld8wdYQAIw1a_RCr2KtgBK7m4_0Hkmd_7WS6BOso5WZgTaQUYJW6-H6h6E-TWNKT6jQg8TU7M3NcVi4CJZJe9FhUp1nbiVxUHucVrQoNveUwy5gNVgZC0UeJfgYw9Qs1wlsQPWZI8Y7gw9ErRU6LMgm-jCQw5dxEu5ev9csLYirjwkJt-aokiedcm8fJ4PIZvCAV19I47Bl5PgNHmqDX5yvUqxghGUWg0VI-nWg0\">OpenFeint</a>. If you’re not familiar, OpenFeint was the first modern mobile gaming network. It launched the year after the iPhone App Store and was part of a game called Aurora Feint. It enabled multiplayer, scoreboards and messaging. The founder of OpenFeint? Jason Citron. Jason’s current startup, that also shares a lot of spiritual luggage with OpenFeint? Discord.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s hard to overstate how important OpenFeint was at the time. As the app ecosystem was emerging it was clear that games would be a big part of what made the iPhone successful and this was the first cross-game network that allowed people to take advantage of one of the first phones to have a persistent, high-quality (ish) internet connection. Apple launched Game Center as a basic response to this need but it has never put any real investment behind it since. Backbone is so good that I could actually see Apple hauling out the repo and assigning engineering talent to get it working well again. The time has come for this idea and Backbone’s execution is so top notch here that it makes the case open and shut.</span></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-2066293\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"461\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png 4780w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png?resize=150,67 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png?resize=300,135 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png?resize=768,345 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png?resize=680,306 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png?resize=1536,691 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png?resize=2048,921 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png?resize=50,22 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I’ve been testing the controller for a few weeks now with a variety of games. I played a quick match of Call of Duty Warzone with Khaira and even though we didn’t secure the dub it was massively more playable than running with touch controls. My very first session of CoD I had a 28 kill game in cod mobile and, even though I was put into a lobby that prioritizes controller users the other players had like 5 kills each. Though you can now pair console controllers to iPhone, the Backbone is so much better than any of the other integrated controllers on the market that it will quickly become a must have for any mobile player that actually wants to be competitive. I have spent as much time with Apple mobile hardware and the people that have created it as probably anyone on the planet so please understand that I don’t say this lightly but this really feels like the game controller and network Apple would have made if it understood competitive games.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Backbone One controller runs $99 and can be </span><a href=\"https://playbackbone.com/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchased via the free Backbone app today</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Panzarino","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_0276.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn32@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-53-36-933_b72f9f4a4b25e303.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.00.51-AM.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn28@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-760_5e564f4857b788e3.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-27-at-9.01.12-AM.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn55@2020_6/2020/10/27/16-54-16-286_c26006ca06a7c81f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn36@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-53-36-082_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn80@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn32@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-14-449_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=7mRqc7pLS64:R_vykjt4Yxc:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn60@2020_6/2020/10/27/16-54-15-396_9e41ab473d58d605.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=7mRqc7pLS64:R_vykjt4Yxc:D7DqB2pKExk":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn14@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-676_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/7mRqc7pLS64":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn99@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-54-14-571_a3c2b0e142ea8f4f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817615707},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","title":"Thanks to COVID-19, emissions and coal use may have peaked in 2019","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2066146","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">If analysts from <a href=\"https://about.bnef.com/\">BloombergNEF</a> are right, then all of the world&#8217;s most greenhouse gas polluting days are behind it, thanks to the COVID-19 pandemic.</p>\n<p>A sharp drop in energy demand caused by the global response to the coronavirus pandemic will remove 2.5 years of energy sector emissions between now and 2050, <a href=\"https://about.bnef.com/new-energy-outlook/\">according to the latest New Energy Outlook from BloombergNEF</a>.</p>\n<p>The latest models from the analysis firm tracking the evolution of the global energy system show that emissions from fuel combustion will likely have peaked in 2019.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The company&#8217;s models show that global emissions declined roughly 20% as a result of the international response to the COVID-19 pandemic, and while those emissions will rise again with economic recoveries, BloombergNEF&#8217;s models never see emissions reaching 2019 levels. And from 2027 emissions are projected to fall at a rate of 0.7% per year to 2050.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2066181\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2066181\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2066181\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"616\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg 1060w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg?resize=150,90 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg?resize=300,181 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg?resize=768,462 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg?resize=680,409 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg?resize=50,30 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2066181\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Bloomberg New Energy Finance chart predicting declines in global emissions. <strong>Image Credit:</strong> <a href=\"https://about.bnef.com/new-energy-outlook/\">BloombergNEF</a></p></div></p>\n<p>These rosy projections are based on the assumption of a massive construction boom for wind and solar power, the adoption of electric vehicles, and improved energy efficiency across industries.</p>\n<p>Together, wind and solar are projected to account for 56% of global electricity generation by mid-century, and along with batteries will gobble up $15.1 trillion invested in new power generation over the next 30 years. The firm also expects another $14 trillion to be invested in the energy grid by 2050.</p>\n<p>The rain on this new energy parade could come from India and China, which have long been reliant on coal power to keep their national economies humming. But even in these colossal coal consumers the Bloomberg report sees good news for people who like good news.</p>\n<p>They expect coal-fired power to peak in China in 2027 and in India in 2030. By 2050, coal is projected to account for only 12% of global electricity consumption. But even with the surge in renewables gas-fired power ain&#8217;t dead. It remains the only fossil-fuel to continue to grow until 2050, albeit at an anemic 0.5% per-year.</p>\n<p>No one should break out the champagne based on these projections, though, because the current trajectory still sees the globe on a course to hit a 3.3 degrees Celsius rise in temperature by 2100.</p>\n<p>“The next ten years will be crucial for the energy transition,&#8221; said Bloomberg New Energy Finance chief executive, Jon Moore. &#8220;There are three key things that we will need to see: accelerated deployment of wind and PV; faster consumer uptake in electric vehicles, small-scale renewables, and low-carbon heating technology, such as heat pumps; and scaled-up development and deployment of zero-carbon fuels.&#8221;</p>\n<p>And a three degree rise in temperature is bad. At that temperature huge swaths of the world would be unlivable because of widespread drought, rainfall in Mexico and Central America would decline by about half, Southern Africa could be exposed to a water crisis and large portions of nations would be covered by sand dunes (including chunks of Botswana and a large portion of the Western U.S.). The Rocky Mountains would be snowless and the Colorado River could be reduce to a stream, according to <a href=\"http://www.climatecodered.org/2010/09/what-would-3-degrees-mean.html#:~:text=Three%20degrees%20would%20likely%20see,to%20fall%2050%20per%20central.\">this description in Climate Code Red.</a></p>\n<p>“To stay well below two degrees of global temperature rise, we would need to reduce emissions by 6% every year starting now, and to limit the warming to 1.5 degrees C, emissions would have to fall by 10% per year,&#8221; Matthias Kimmel, a senior analyst and co-author of the latest report, said in a statement.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=6N9jRi2rf98:eQdJZhVCV3g:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=6N9jRi2rf98:eQdJZhVCV3g:7Q72WNTAKBA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=6N9jRi2rf98:eQdJZhVCV3g:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=6N9jRi2rf98:eQdJZhVCV3g:-BTjWOF_DHI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=6N9jRi2rf98:eQdJZhVCV3g:-BTjWOF_DHI\" +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg","linkMd5":"7090d05f501b6869d4077037ac94aff7","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn39@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-10-701_3cdc4a14bfc698e1.webp","destWidth":1060,"destHeight":638,"sourceBytes":66993,"destBytes":28508,"author":"Jonathan Shieber","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/unnamed-1-1.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn39@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-10-701_3cdc4a14bfc698e1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn36@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-53-36-082_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn80@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-668_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn32@2020_5/2020/10/27/16-54-14-449_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=6N9jRi2rf98:eQdJZhVCV3g:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn43@2020_3/2020/10/27/16-54-15-463_07e05b8d62077fbb.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=6N9jRi2rf98:eQdJZhVCV3g:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn29@2020_4/2020/10/27/16-54-15-909_d52952300342819e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn14@2020_2/2020/10/27/16-54-15-676_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/6N9jRi2rf98":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn40@2020_6/2020/10/27/16-54-15-462_1d925e7d393ff08b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1603817615705},{"createdTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","updatedTime":"2020-10-28 00:53:35","title":"Next-gen skincare, silk without spiders and pollution for lunch: Meet the biotech startups pitching at IndieBio’s Demo Day","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2066155","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Biotech can often, and sometimes literally, fly over our heads. However, the pandemic has shown an increased need for investment and focus on solutions that work on human and planetary health. For <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/synbio-axlr8r\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"synbio-axlr8r\">IndieBio, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> a science and biotech accelerator run by VC firm SOSV, this unprecedented year offered high stakes and new challenges.</p>\n<p>Today and tomorrow, the biotech accelerator is hosting its twice-annual demo day.</p>\n<p>Starting in 2015, IndieBio has provided resources to founders solving complex challenges with biotech, from fake meat to sustainability. Over the years, the accelerator has created a portfolio of biotech companies valued at over <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/15/leaving-the-3-2-billion-portfolio-he-helped-build-at-indiebio-arvind-gupta-joins-mayfield-to-create-the-genesis-consortium/\">$3.2 billion</a>, including companies like Memphis Meats, which develops cultured meat from animal cells; NotCo, a plant-based food brand; and Catalog, which uses organisms for data storage.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"uT28iYUKBX\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/15/leaving-the-3-2-billion-portfolio-he-helped-build-at-indiebio-arvind-gupta-joins-mayfield-to-create-the-genesis-consortium/\">Leaving the $3.2 billion portfolio he helped build at IndieBio, Arvind Gupta joins Mayfield to create the Genesis Consortium</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Leaving the $3.2 billion portfolio he helped build at IndieBio, Arvind Gupta joins Mayfield to create the Genesis Consortium&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/15/leaving-the-3-2-billion-portfolio-he-helped-build-at-indiebio-arvind-gupta-joins-mayfield-to-create-the-genesis-consortium/embed/#?secret=uT28iYUKBX\" data-secret=\"uT28iYUKBX\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>As part of the accelerator, each participating company receives $250,000 in capital, numerous other services and access to lab space. In July, the founder and head of IndieBio, Arvind Gupta, left his position to pursue a role at Mayfield. While Gupta remains an adviser, Po Bronson took the role as the new managing director.</p>\n<p>Bronson was immediately put to the test. This year, the program expanded from operating solely in San Francisco to also create a cohort based in New York. It also doubled the amount of companies it invested in, bringing this cohort to 20 companies.</p>\n<p>As you can imagine, lockdowns ultimately forced founders to delay key lab work in the beginning of the pandemic. Eventually, founders were able to partner with universities, contract research organizations or other biotech accelerators to begin their research, says Maya Lockwood, the head of investor relations at SOSV. The NYC class received a “golden ticket” for free lab space come November.</p>\n<p>And these dynamics make this cohort all the more fascinating to dive into.</p>\n<p>Watch the New York Stream <a href=\"https://sosv.com/preview/indiebio-demo-day-2020-ny-community\">here</a>, which will happen on Tuesday October 27 from 1:00-3:00pm ET.</p>\n<p>Watch the San Francisco stream <a href=\"https://sosv.com/preview/indiebio-demo-day-2020-sf-community\">here</a>, which will happen on Wednesday October 28 from 10:00-12:00pm PT.</p>\n<p>For those who can’t tune in, here’s a list of all the companies presenting in New York and San Francisco over the next two days.</p>\n<h2>San Francisco cohort</h2>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://reazent.com/\">Reazent:</a> </strong>Founded by Sumit Verma, Reazent has discovered and patented a way to manipulate soil bacteria into triggering crops to grow more. It works with 116 strains, from kale to potatoes, and wants to dig into the market of organic agricultural land.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1911601\" style=\"width: 746px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1911601\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\" wp-image-1911601\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg\" alt=\"seedlings sprouts plants\" width=\"736\" height=\"491\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg 2120w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg?resize=2048,1366 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/GettyImages-953168856.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 736px) 100vw, 736px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1911601\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Witthaya Prasongsin / Getty Images</p></div></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.krakensense.com/\"><strong>Kraken Sense: </strong></a>Founded by Nisha Sarveswaran, Kraken Sense has created an in-line autonomous device to measure the concentration of pathogens in large-scale food and water systems. The product can be deployed in farms and kitchens and uses refillable single-use cartridges.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.advancedmicrobubbles.com/\"><strong>Advanced Microbubbles:</strong></a> The startup, led by Jameel Feshitan, has created a platform that helps practitioners deliver drugs to complex and difficult tumors. The company collaborated with NIH NIDA and uses proprietary bubbles to deliver chemotherapeutics. Currently, Microbubbles is working to solve two types of cancers: neuroblastoma and pancreatic cancer.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://cybelemicrobiome.com/\"><strong>Cybele Microbiome:</strong></a> CEO Nicole Scott has created a direct-to-consumer skincare line with a focus on prebiotics. The line uses ingredients that work in tandem with the skin microbiome, even triggering it to express natural scents.</p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.ivynatal.com/\">Ivy Natal:</a></strong> Ivy Natal is developing a process to harvest healthy human egg cells from skin cells. CEO Colin Bortner is working on a treatment for infertility and plans to enable families to have genetic children who can’t otherwise with current solutions.</p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://indiebio.co/microgenesis-fertility-biome/\">Microgenesis:</a> </strong>Led by Gabriela Gutierrez, Microgenesis has created a proprietary test and nutraceutical regiment (including probiotics) to help women who struggle with infertility get pregnant. The company worked with a cohort of 287 mothers, and with its product over 75% of patients became pregnant.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1759391\" style=\"width: 757px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1759391\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\" wp-image-1759391\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"747\" height=\"498\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg 6993w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg?resize=768,513 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg?resize=680,454 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg?resize=1536,1025 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg?resize=2048,1367 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/GettyImages-556450831.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 747px) 100vw, 747px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1759391\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Westend61 / Getty Images</p></div></p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.asimica.com/\">AsimicA:</a></strong> Led by Nikolai Mushnikov, Asmicia has created a new way to bring stem cells to microbes. The company could lengthen and grow the yields of bio-manufacturing, and is currently working to select the right fermentation partner.</p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"http://www.liberumbio.com/\">Liberum:</a></strong> CEO Aiden Tinafar is working to disrupt what they think could be a $400 billion market opportunity: recombinant proteins. Liberum has created a protein printer that could cut down the creation of custom recombinant proteins from weeks to a few hours.</p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.khepra.xyz/\">Khepra:</a> </strong>Led by Julie Kring, Khepra is leveraging fuel production as a way to store extra renewable energy. The company is building a series of reactors that could take your old plastic bottles and cardboard boxes, extract chemicals and fuels, and sell that fuel to refineries.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.carbixcorp.com/\"><strong>Carbix:</strong></a> Carbix, led by Quincy Sammy, takes enriched CO2 and converts it into raw material that can then be repurposed into industrial products.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.spintex.co.uk/\"><strong>Spintext:</strong></a> CEO Alex Greenhalgh is creating a new, scalable way of making silk. The company mimics spider spinning and uses a natural protein, with an end product that they see as better than premium silk.</p>\n<h2><strong>New York cohort</strong></h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.biomage.net/\"><strong>Biomage:</strong></a> CEO Adam Kurkiewicz wants to make single-cell sequencing data more accessible for research biologistics. The technology could help scientists explore human cells to enhance medicine and drug discovery.</p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://diptera.ai/\">Diptera.ai:</a></strong> Vic Levitin is creating a scalable, affordable and sustainable way to fight mosquitoes and their diseases.</p>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.cayugabiotech.com/\">Cayuga Biotech:</a></strong> Damien Kudela, CEO of Cayuga Biotech, has created a drug that could induce clots and stop severe bleeding situations.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.bcure.co.uk/\"><strong>Brightcure:</strong></a> Chiara Heide, CEO of Brightcure, has created a bioactive cream that uses natural bacterium to restore a woman’s natural microbiome.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.multus.media/\"><strong>Multus Media:</strong></a> CEO Cai Linton is producing an ingredient that hopes to make cultivated meat production affordable and accessible.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2026211\" style=\"width: 828px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2026211\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\" wp-image-2026211\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/GettyImages-1261086485.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"818\" 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/GettyImages-1261086485.jpg?resize=2048,1024 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/GettyImages-1261086485.jpg?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 818px) 100vw, 818px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2026211\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Getty Images</p></div></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.biofeyn.com/\"><strong>BioFeyn:</strong></a> The company uses nanotechnologies based on human medicine to deliver nutrients and disease prevention to fish. CEO Timothy Bouley is working to make eating healthy fish a sustainable practice.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.halomine.com/\"><strong>Halomine:</strong></a> Ted Eveleth, CEO, wants to turn every surface into an antimicrobial surface. Halomine’s product, Halofilm, can be used in tandem with any household bleach cleaner to enhance disinfection techniques.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.alliedmicrobiota.com/\"><strong>Allied Microbiota:</strong></a><strong> </strong>Lauralynn Kourtz, CEO of Allied Microbiota, wants to use natural microbes to eliminate toxic waste. The company uses bacteria to clean contaminated soils.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://scindo.bio/\"><strong>Scindo:</strong></a> Scindo, led by Gustaf Hemberg, uses enzymes to make plastic biodegradable.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"fysCQZfI6y\"><p><a
